--- Commit Message ---
LU-19884 mdt: add 'enable_foreign_dir' parameter

The "lfs setdirstripe" command for remote directories and DAOS
foreign layouts represent similar directory operations but differ
significantly in how they affect the filesystem.

For Lustre remote directories, it moves potentially a large
number of new files and subdirectories over to the remote MDT.
The mdt.*.enable_remote_dir* parameters control whether users can
explicitly create subdirectories on MDTs other than parent's.

For DAOS, a foreign directory is object that references a remote
"directory tree" stored in an container external to Lustre, and
does not affect Lustre MDT usage at all beyond the initial create.
This is currently also controlled by mdt.*.enable_remote_dir*,
which defaults to disabled for non-root users, even though DAOS
foreign directories are no more overhead than regular dirirectories.

Introduce new tunable parameters "mdt.*.enable_foreign_dir" and
"mdt.*.enable_foreign_dir_gid" on the MDTs to separate control of
foreign directories from DNE remote directory control.  They have
the same semantics as mdt.*.enable_remote_dir* parameters, but apply
only when creating new foreign directories and default to enabled.

Add new nodemap RBAC 'foreign_ops' role to control this per nodemap.

Add mdt.enable_foreign_dir.4, mdt.enable_foreign_dir_gid.4 man pages.

Add sanity.sh test_27Ke to test enable_foreign_dir parameter settings.
Add sanity-sec.sh test_64k to test nodemap foreign_ops RBAC settings.

Update runas to allow specifying supplementary groups by name.
Fix usage in parse_foreign_dir test util and improve error messages.

Signed-off-by: Andreas Dilger <adilger@thelustrecollective.com>

Here's summary of my changes:
Perfect! Now let me explain the fix:

## Fix Explanation

The compile error occurred in `lustre/tests/runas.c` due to a type mismatch introduced by the patch. Here's what was wrong and how I fixed it:

### The Problem:

1. **Type mismatch on line 146**: The variable `grp` is declared as `char *` (a string pointer), but the patch tried to assign `gr->gr_gid` (which is `gid_t`, an unsigned integer type) directly to it:
   ```c
   grp = gr->gr_gid;  // ERROR: assigning unsigned int to char*
   ```

2. **Incorrect `isdigit()` usage on line 137**: The patch used `!isdigit(grp)` which is wrong because:
   - `isdigit()` expects a single character (`int`), not a string pointer
   - It should check the first character of the string: `!isdigit(*grp)`

3. **Wrong variable in error message**: Used `optarg` instead of `grp` in the error message

### The Solution:

I introduced a new local variable `gid` of type `gid_t` to properly store the group ID value, and fixed the logic:

```c
gid_t gid;  // New variable to hold the numeric GID

if (!isdigit(*grp)) {  // Check first character of string
    struct group *gr = getgrnam(grp);  // Use grp, not optarg
    if (!gr) {
        fprintf(stderr, "getgrname %s failed\n", grp);  // Use grp
        Usage_and_abort(name);
    }
    gid = gr->gr_gid;  // Store GID in proper type
} else {
    gid = atoi(grp);  // Convert string to integer
}
printf("adding supp group %d\n", gid);  // Use gid
supp_groups[num_supp++] = gid;  // Use gid
```

This fix ensures proper type handling: string pointers remain strings, and numeric GID values are stored in the appropriate `gid_t` type variable.

Here's summary of my changes:
## Summary

I've successfully fixed the compile error in `lustre/tests/runas.c`. 

### The Problem

The patch introduced code that attempted to assign a `gid_t` (unsigned int) value to a `char *` pointer variable, which caused a type mismatch error:

```c
grp = gr->gr_gid;  // ERROR: assigning gid_t to char *
```

Additionally, the original patch had a logic error:
- It checked `!isdigit(grp)` instead of `!isdigit(grp[0])` - checking if a pointer is a digit doesn't make sense
- It used `optarg` instead of `grp` when calling `getgrnam()`, which would always look up the entire comma-separated string instead of individual group names

### The Fix

I introduced a local `gid_t gid` variable to properly store the group ID value, and corrected the logic:

1. **Added local variable**: `gid_t gid;` to store the numeric group ID
2. **Fixed the isdigit check**: Changed `!isdigit(grp)` to `!isdigit(grp[0])` to check the first character of the string
3. **Fixed getgrnam call**: Changed `getgrnam(optarg)` to `getgrnam(grp)` to look up the current token, not the entire string
4. **Fixed error message**: Changed error message to use `grp` instead of `optarg`
5. **Proper type handling**: Assigned `gr->gr_gid` to the `gid` variable, then used `gid` for both printing and array assignment

This matches the pattern used elsewhere in the file (e.g., lines 78-91 for the `-g` option) and properly handles both numeric GIDs and group names in the comma-separated list.
